>     - ­¤¤ó **STEP 2 / the DO-WHILE-WITH-SWITCH residue pair ($8C88, $B6D6) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-04 (commits `19701a7`, `4104bc6`).** The two shapes the step-2 finish-line flagged as a deferred follow-on, now folded ŌĆö and they turned out to be TWO distinct sub-shapes, each its own one-line-of-machinery fix gated by CFG-equivalence: **(1) interleaved-pure-exit do-while ($8C88 `draw_unit_roster_columns`):** a clean bottom-test do-while whose listing span contains an *unrelated* exit-path block (`$8CCB`, reached only from the post-loop exit path). `_fold_dowhile` previously hard-bailed on ANY interleaved non-loop block; now it ALLOWS interleaved PURE-EXIT blocks but ŌĆö UNLIKE `_fold_while` ŌĆö does NOT relocate them. **KEY LESSON (cost me a wrong first attempt): the lowering's merge/fall computations are ADDRESS-based (lexical order assumed to track address order), so relocating a block to an address-inconsistent lexical slot is UNSOUND** ŌĆö a relocate-to-end attempt made `structure_lines`' `if(arg1){}` merge resolve to `EXIT` instead of the moved block (the gate caught it). Left in place, the block renders inside the do-body reached by an honest *backward* goto (which `structure_lines` won't mis-fold ŌĆö Patterns A/B are forward-only); CFG stays exact. **(2) while(1)-with-conditional-exit ($B6D6 `command_menu_select_loop`, +$AB29 `render_arms_edit_screen` bonus):** the test-in-the-MIDDLE menu loop ŌĆö a switch-header loop whose conditional back edge `if(C) goto L_h` sits mid-listing with case bodies laid out AFTER it (do-while can't express it; the test isn't the last loop line). Relaxed `_fold_while1`'s belt-and-suspenders conditional-back-edge bail to ATTEMPT the fold when the back edge's NON-continue branch is a PURE-EXIT `return`/`break` ŌĆö so `if(C) continue; return ŌĆ”;` exits correctly (NOT the do-while-loops-wrongly GATE HOLE that step-2(c) closed). Safe by TWO independent mechanisms: dispatch (a plain bottom-test do-while is intercepted by `_fold_dowhile` first ŌĆö $830B proves this, never reaches `_fold_while1`) AND the gate (already proven sound vs the bad while(1) by the $830B test). **$AC11/$AC33 needed NO work ŌĆö already a `while(1)` from step 2(c)** (the residual `goto L_AC33` is a switch CASE default = Phase-3 territory, which over-flagged my triage). Gates per commit: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, drift-guard CLEAN, `--check` 0 BAD ├Ś4, decompiled diff a pure structural transform (`git diff -w`: only do/while(1)/continue/-goto/-L_label). **test-vm-cfg 56ŌåÆ65**: $8C61 in the do-while suite (its `fold ~= raw` is the regression guard for interleaved-pure-exit ŌĆö it FAILED pre-fix) + $B6B4/$AB22 each get folded-while(1)+if-continue / fold~=raw / **if-continueŌåÆbreak REJECTED** (proves the continue TARGET is checked, the soundness the relaxation rests on).
>     - ­¤¤ó **STEP 3 = the genuine two-test (`both`) loops ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-04. 5 of the 6 named subs fold + 9 bonus do-whiles (14 new do-whiles total), every gate green, ZERO new fallbacks.** The insight that collapsed the whole class: a two-test `both` loop is **just a do-while whose HEADER also carries an exit-test** ŌĆö so route it to `_fold_dowhile` and let the existing `_emit_break_continue` post-pass rewrite the header's in-loop `goto L_exit` ŌåÆ `if (C) break;`. NO bespoke `_fold_while`-with-conditional-tail needed. Three small, each gate-driven, fixes: **(1) dispatch** ŌĆö new `elif utest and htest and u != h` branch in `structure_loops` routes the `both` shape to `_fold_dowhile` (which self-validates + the CFG gate is the backstop). **(2) flushed-call HOIST in `_fold_dowhile`** ŌĆö the button-wait archetype (`prompt_yes_no $822A`, `ui_helper_d3a7 $D3A7`, `ui_helper_d351 $D351`) emits a discarded-return CALL (`read_frame_timer(1)`) AFTER the `L_h:` label but tagged with its earlier, PRE-HEADER address; its block is the pre-loop entry, so leaving it in the do-body splits the entry block across the loop boundary ŌåÆ gate (correctly) rejected. Fix: hoist any in-span line with `addr < h` + non-leader (= a flushed side-effect, control lines keep their position) OUT to before `do {` ŌĆö the SAFE relocation direction (to an address-CONSISTENT slot below h, the opposite of the $8C88 move-to-end that was unsound). **(3) `vm_cfg.lower_struct_cfg` loop_ctx ROOT FIX** ŌĆö the do-while path `discard`ed the header block `hb` from the loop context, so a `break` INSIDE the header block (the defining feature of a two-test loop, never seen before) couldn't resolve to the exit ŌåÆ the header lost its exit edge (gate divergence `struct $823BŌåÆ{$8245}` vs `rawŌåÆ{$8245,$824D}`). Now KEEP `hb` in loop_ctx; harmless for plain do-whiles (no header break) + self-loops (special-cased via dowhile_edges first). **Result: $822A/$8FEC/$D351/$D3A7/$E554 fold** (the 6th, `$AF3B`, correctly stays an if/else `gated_fallback`); $D351 proves MULTIPLE header breaks resolve (`if(==64) break; if(==128) break;`). Reads as source: `prompt_yes_no` = `read_frame_timer(1); do { local11 = wait_button_edge(); if (ŌĆ” == 64) break; } while (local11 != 128);`. Loop totals now **88** (60 top-test while + 25 do-while + 3 while1). Gates: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, drift-guard CLEAN, `--check` 0 BAD ├Ś4, decompiled diff a pure structural transform (`git diff -w`: only +do/+}while/-goto/-L_label + one legit if/else re-render in the bonus `seek_enemy_adjacent_cell_and_commit_move`). **test-vm-cfg 65ŌåÆ74**: $822A/$D3A7/$D351 each get folded-two-test-do-while+header-break / fold~=raw / **header breakŌåÆcontinue (exitŌåÆheader) REJECTED** (proves the header break's EXIT target is checked ŌĆö the soundness the loop_ctx-header fix rests on). Ō¢Č Remaining loop frontier = the **68 multi-HEADER nested/sibling subs** (the big separate bucket) + Phase 3 switch-body inlining. ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ **Surfaced (NOT caused) a foundational decompiler bug ŌĆö see Inbox `Ō¢Č DECOMPILER BUG ŌĆö compare opcodes $C3/$C5/$C6 render INVERTED direction`**: the bonus `seek_enemyŌĆ”` folds to `} while (local11 >= 6)` which is faithful to the decompiler's (buggy) condition but semantically should be `< 6`; the fold is CFG-correct, the wrongness is the orthogonal compare-primitive bug present in goto form too.
>     - Ō£ģ **STEP 2 COMPLETE 2026-06-04. $9A0F RESOLVED as a sanctioned honest goto ŌĆö and it's the LONE one.** Census (`single-header Ōēź2-back-edge loops still without a while/do construct`) returns **exactly 1 across all 4 banks: `$99D2`/`$9A0F` `ai_place_combat_units_random_or_smart`** ŌĆö every other step-2-class menu loop is folded. `$9A0F` is genuinely unfoldable *soundly*: it's a FULLY-ROTATED multi-back-edge loop ŌĆö the header `$9A0F` (which also does the per-iteration `commit_unit_move_and_redraw_count(rng,rng)` work) sits at the **highest** address while its real body-entry `$99F9` is laid out **after** the `slot++` continue block `$99EF`. A top-test `while` resolves the body-entry to the listing-first block (`$99EF`) instead of the bytecode entry (`$99F9`) ŌåÆ the gate REJECTS it (divergence `struct $9A0FŌåÆ$99EF` vs `rawŌåÆ$99F9`); fixing it would need body REORDERING, which the $8C88 work proved is unsound under the address-based lowering. `while(1)` doesn't fit either (the header must OPEN the span ŌĆö `_fold_while1` line 1511 ŌĆö but it's at the bottom of the address range). So it correctly reverts to honest goto (one of the 35 fallbacks). This is exactly the EPIC's "leave an honest goto where the bytecode layout is genuinely tangled ŌĆö correct, not a failure." **The whole step-2 menu-loop class is now folded or honestly-goto'd; Ō¢Č the remaining loop frontier is STEP 3 (the 6 two-test `both` loops above) + the 68 multi-HEADER nested/sibling subs (the big separate bucket).** [[feedback_transpilation_as_grounding]]
> - ­¤¤ó **Phase 3 ŌĆö `switch` body inlining ŌĆö STEP 1 DONE 2026-06-04. ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ KEY FINDING: "only 3 clean" was a measurement error ŌĆö the real prize is 29/38.** The metric was wrong: C `switch` does fall-through NATIVELY (and this VM's switch is first-class ŌĆö `$D5`/`$D9`), so the test is **single-entry dispatch** (every case target dominated by the switch block ŌåÆ the bodies can move INSIDE the braces), NOT "break-separated bodies." By that test **29 of 38 switches are FORMALIZABLE**; only **9 stay goto-cases** (a case body entered from OUTSIDE the switch ŌĆö irreducible; 8 of them are the step-2 `while(1)` menu loops where `continue` re-enters a case). Survey tool `tools/probe-switch-shapes.py`. **Chris's call (option 1): formalize EVERY single-entry switch ŌĆö bodies inside the braces, honest internal `goto` local to the case where fall-through can't reach** (vs only folding pure-break ones). **STEP 1 landed 12 of the 25 the detector finds** (the interleaved-merge ones, which converge via goto and need no `break`): the shared detector `vm_cfg.switch_dispatches` (single-entry test + S-dominated enclosed span; **both** the emit and the gate consume it, so they can't disagree ŌĆö the `value_diamonds` pattern) ŌåÆ `vm_decompile.structure_switches` (runs LAST, after loops+if/else, so it never reorders body lines: lexical order == address order is preserved, keeping the address-based gate faithful AND the C correct) drops the `case N: goto L_X` dispatch lines, moves the bodies inside the braces with inline `case N:`/`default:` labels, prunes the now-unreferenced case-target labels ŌåÆ `vm_cfg.lower_struct_cfg` reads the switch header's successors from the inline `case` labels (`switch_edges`, parallel to `header_edges`/`dowhile_edges`). **Three real traps caught + handled:** (a) body cut off mid-block (`brace_close` is the last block's LEADER, not its end ŌåÆ added `body_end`); (b) the lexical-vs-address gap ŌĆö `structure_lines` folds an `if{}` whose braces cross a `case:` boundary and swallow the next case (`$95BE`, legal-but-ugly Duff's-device C the address gate would accept) ŌåÆ a **lexical-foldability guard** (every case target must sit at brace-depth 0) skips those, leaving them honest goto-cases; (c) a switch fold that breaks the gate now PROGRESSIVELY falls back (drop switch ŌåÆ drop loop+switch ŌåÆ goto) so it never costs a sub its other valid folds. **Reads as source now:** `per_period_fief_daimyo_update_driver` ($A30D) = `switch(current_season){ case 1: highwater reset; case 2: harvest; case 3: relations decay; case 0/default: aging }`. Gates ALL green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED ŌĆö zero regression**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, --check 0 BAD ├Ś4, drift CLEAN, decompiled diff is a pure structural transform (`git diff -w`: +`case`/+`}`/ŌłÆ`goto L_X`/ŌłÆ`L_X:`). **Non-vacuousness PROVEN** ŌĆö `test-vm-cfg.py` 94ŌåÆ**106**: a dropped case label (lost dispatch edge) is REJECTED (existential ŌĆö a router-shared case is genuinely CFG-neutral, contraction absorbs it; the gate is right to accept that). Ō¢Č STEP 2 = the clean-trailing-merge switches (the fall-through ladders). Ō¢Č STEP 3 = the nested-case-target switches.
>   - ­¤¤ó **STEP 2 DONE 2026-06-04 ŌĆö the fall-through ladders, +4 (12ŌåÆ16 of 25). KEY: no `break` keyword needed.** A case targeting the trailing merge M (== `body_end`, the block right AFTER the `}`) is emitted as an **EMPTY trailing case that falls through the `}` to M** ŌĆö fall-off-the-switch IS break semantics, and the address-based gate already models it as a fall to `body_end`, so NO `break;` keyword and NO switch break-context in the gate were needed (simpler than the loop break substrate). One change in `structure_switches`: after the body walk, any case target not placed inside the territory but equal to `body_end` gets an empty `case`/`default:` label before the `}`. **`ai_terrain_strength_term` ($9BB4) now reads as the textbook ladder** ŌĆö `local11 = 3; switch(terrain){ case 32: local11--; case 16: local11--; case 8: local11--; default: } return ŌĆ”` (`= 3 ŌłÆ count`). Gates green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**35 fallbacks UNCHANGED**), round-trip CLEAN, --check 0 BAD, drift CLEAN, test-vm-cfg **106** ($9BB4 ladder added as a fixture: folds + a dropped ladder case is REJECTED). Ō¢Č STEP 3 = the remaining 9.
>   - ­¤¤ó **STEP 3 DONE 2026-06-04 ŌĆö the fold BARRIER, +2 (16ŌåÆ18 of 25) AND fallbacks improved 35ŌåÆ34.** `structure_lines` gained a `case_barriers` param (the switch case-target addresses, computed from `switch_dispatches` before it runs): a braced `if{}`/`if-else` fold whose body `[i+1, fold_end)` would ENCLOSE a case target is suppressed ŌåÆ that case target stays at brace-depth 0 so `structure_switches` can inline the switch (the local `if` just keeps its goto). **Freed `$95BE` (the malformed-Duff's-device case from step 1) and `$A2D2` (was a gate-reject ŌåÆ now folds cleanly, hence one FEWER fallback than baseline).** Diff is a pure structural transform (`git diff -w` = only `case`/`default:`/`}`/`goto`/`L_`/`switch`/`if (` tokens ŌĆö the barrier reverts a few if-folds to goto, both faithful). Gates green: cfg-gate 495/495 + 495/495 (**34 fallbacks**), round-trip 495/45024 CLEAN, --check 0 BAD ├Ś4, drift CLEAN, test-vm-cfg 106. **Ō¢ČŌ¢Č PHASE 3 SUBSTANTIALLY COMPLETE ŌĆö 18 of 25 detected switches inlined (and 9 of 38 total were always honest goto: a case body entered from outside the switch).** The **7 residue** (`$8A4E`,`$8DFD`,`$ADF6`,`$8488` + the `while(1)`-nested `$AB22`,`$AC11`,`$B6B4`) are switches nested INSIDE an outer `if{}`/`while{}` where the switch's territory boundary collides with the OUTER closing braces (addr-0 scaffold the address-based body-walk can't attribute to switch-vs-outer) ŌĆö folding them soundly needs a brace-aware `structure_switches` (track nesting, place the switch `}` relative to outer braces), a real redesign for diminishing returns. They correctly **stay honest goto-cases** ŌĆö the epic's sanctioned "leave a goto where the bytecode/layout is genuinely tangled." [[feedback_transpilation_as_grounding]]
> - **Success = "reads like C, with a few honest gotos where the bytecode genuinely is spaghetti."** Each phase measured by goto-reduction count; each commit gated by CFG-equivalence + the existing round-trip/--check/drift-guard staying green (those still apply ŌĆö bytecode & disasm are untouched; only the C *rendering* changes). ### EPIC: "See the whole picture" ŌĆö full bytecodeŌåÆC decode, PERSISTED
> The core gap (Chris, 2026-05-29): **the C decompiler output is never stored ŌĆö we regenerate it every session.** It's deterministic (fixed ROM ŌåÆ identical C forever), so re-deriving it is pure waste ŌĆö the SRT-cleaning tell on the project's most valuable output. The fix this whole restructure was designed for: **decompile once, commit the `.c`, read it like a codebase.**
> Status verified 2026-05-29: VM-disasm covers only **4 of 16 banks** (00/01/02/15); C decompile is per-subroutine and ephemeral. No persisted whole-bank C exists.
- [x] 1. Recover/rebuild `vm-disasm.py` and save it. **DONE 2026-05-30** ŌĆö `tools/vm-disasm.py`, built on execution-validated `OPCODE_INFO` lengths + handler-decoded `$D5`/`$D9` variable-length switches + recursive-descent reachability termination. Validated by **exact-tiling** (the 135/131/131/98 stubs must tile each bank): **0 misaligned across all 495 subs**.
- [x] 2. Dump banks **03ŌĆō14** ŌåÆ reveal code-vs-data split. **DONE / COLLAPSED 2026-05-30** ŌĆö surprise finding: **banks 03ŌĆō14 are almost entirely DATA.** Stub counts: banks 3-9,11-13 = **0**, bank 10 (audio) = 1, bank 14 = 3. **All ~495 bytecode subs live in banks 0/1/2/15** ŌĆö which are already dumped (and hand-annotated). There is no 12-banks-of-bytecode to dump; the engine's *code* is 4 banks, the other 12 are graphics/maps/text/tables. **This is the big reframe: the epic is mostly already done, it just wasn't named.**
- [x] 3a. **`vm_decompile.py` ported to be spec-agnostic ŌĆö DONE 2026-05-30.** Instead of keying on the old mnemonic strings, dispatch now normalizes the mnemonic from the **opcode byte** (`OPCODE_TO_MNEMONIC`, 256-entry) ŌĆö so it consumes EITHER the old hand-annotated files OR fresh `vm-disasm.py` v2 output, same C from both. Also matched the signed-decimal immediate rendering ($89/$8B/$8D/$8F/$AE) in `vm-disasm.py`. Validated against bank 1: **58/131 subs byte-identical** old-vs-new; the other 73 differ ONLY because the new tool has **correct lengths** (49 subs) or **live labels** (24 subs) ŌĆö the decompile *logic* is identical, and grow reproduces its formula exactly. The prereq for decompile-all is cleared.
- [x] 3b. **decompile-all driver ŌĆö DONE 2026-05-30** (`tools/decompile-all.py`). Runs vm-disasm(v2) ŌåÆ vm_decompile over the 4 code banks, captures per-sub C, writes `decompiled/bank_NN.c`. **495 subs, ~11.8k lines.**

The "data interleaved with code" blocker is solved (`$D5`/`$D9` inline jump tables length-decoded in `vm-disasm.py`).
- **DRIFT NOTE (do NOT silently regenerate the 4 hand-annotated banks):** the committed `disasm/{bank_00,01,02,15}_vm.asm` carry hand corrections, resolved string literals, address labels, and a summary footer ŌĆö more valuable than a fresh dump. They also still drive `vm_decompile.py`. Regenerating them with the v2-mnemonic tool would destroy curation **and** break the decompiler until step 3's port lands. The recovered tool is for *fresh* analysis / re-validation, not for clobbering these. The old files' remaining length bugs ($84/$A0/$AA/ŌĆ”) are documented in `vm-disasm.py`'s header ŌĆö fix them in place during the v2 port if anyone re-derives from those files.

### EPIC: 50-fief map data from ROM (not SRAM) ŌĆö REScOPED 2026-05-29
> Goal unchanged: render all 50 maps without hand-capturing 50 SRAM dumps. But the premise changed.
> **Verified finding ([[project_nobunaga_cell_encoding_vm]], re-confirmed 2026-05-29; refined 2026-05-30):** there is NO static *whole-map* table. Tactical maps are **emitted byte-by-byte by per-fief VM bytecode at battle init** (sub `$8903` reads a metatile byte ŌåÆ `memcpy_banked` ŌåÆ `$7BFD`). The bank-4 `$A57E` table IS the live **per-cell metatile source** (`$8903` reads it one byte at a time, indexed by computed offset) ŌĆö but `render-atlas.py`'s reading of it as a *directly renderable whole-map* was the dead-end; that renderer stays ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ INVALIDATED. The correct path is to run `$8903`, not to read `$A57E` flat.
> **The unblock:** the 2026-05-21 memory scoped the programmatic path as "multi-day ŌĆö build a partial VM interpreter." **That interpreter now exists** (`nobunaga_vm.py`, the one that cracked math32).
>
> **PROGRESS 2026-05-29 ŌĆö ROMŌåÆSRAM emit routine LOCATED + partially decoded:**
> - Key finding: the captured `*-combat-init.txt.gz` traces are **render-phase (SRAMŌåÆPPU), taken AFTER the map was loaded** ŌĆö they contain ZERO staging-buffer writes. That's *why* ROMŌåÆSRAM was never decoded; no existing artifact holds it. It had to be found in code.
> - The emit routine is **bank-2 VM sub `$885E`** (also `$8942`; confirms the memory's `$894A` lead). It loops 5 rows, computes `dest = $7BFD + ŌĆ”┬Ę88 + offset` (88 = the known col stride), and `host_call $CC54` does the metatile-pattern copy.
> - `vm_decompile.py` of `$885E` shows the **map source is selected by `$6F63` (defending province = which fief's map) + `$6FFE` (mode), via pointers around `$B540`ŌĆō`$B547` (bank 2)**. So the per-fief map table is `$B540`-area, province-indexed ŌĆö NOT the disproven bank-4 `$A57E`.
- [ ] 1. Characterize the `$B540`-area table (pointer table? per-fief encoding?) + decode `host_call $CC54` (the metatile copy). This is the remaining ROMŌåÆSRAM unknown.
- [x] **Syscall layer built + working** (`probe-map-emit.py`, 2026-05-29/30). Intercepts `host_call $F226`, reads the param struct from the VM stack (`$02/$03`=`vm_sp`; `struct[0]`=task id ŌĆö NOT the host_call adj byte, which is the struct-pop size), dispatches by task id. With it the emit path runs **clean, no hang** (the earlier crashes were just unresolved syscalls ŌĆö `wait_for_nmi` spinning, the blit losing sync). Decoded syscalls so far: `$10` memcpy_banked, `$11` rng_next, `$13` wait_for_nmi (stub), **`$14` ppu_blit_from_bank** ($C428: reads tile bytes from SRAM pointer `struct[12]` ŌåÆ writes `PPUDATA`). Unknown ids auto-stub + log ŌåÆ fill in the ~32 over time. **Promote this layer into `nobunaga_vm` next** (it's reusable core capability).
- [!] **COURSE CORRECTION (2026-05-30): `$885E` is the RENDER driver (SRAM staging ŌåÆ PPU), NOT the ROMŌåÆSRAM populator.** It was found via its `$7BFD` references, but those are *reads* ŌĆö it walks the staging buffer ($7BFD + col*88) and blits each column to PPU via task `$14` (which reads `struct[12]`=`$7D05` staging ptr ŌåÆ `PPUDATA`). In the Mino dump the staging buffer was *already* populated (1048 nonzero) before `$885E` ran. So the actual ROMŌåÆSRAM step is a **different, still-unfound routine.**
- [x] 2'. **POPULATOR = bank-2 sub `$8903` ŌĆö WORKING 2026-05-30.** Battle-init driver `$AFE1` calls `$8903` (populate) at `$AFFC`, then `$8977`ŌåÆ`$885E` (render) at `$AFFF`. Run `probe-map-emit.py traces/mino-save-ram.dmp 8903`: returns clean (`ok=True, depth=0`), fires only `memcpy_banked` ├Ś110, and reproduces **880/988 (89%) of the cell-grid region `$7BFD-$7FFF`** (up from 2). Three fixes unlocked it:
  1. **`call_bank ($07)` implemented** (see Open above) ŌĆö was derailing the whole run.
  2. **`memcpy_banked` param offsets were wrong** ŌĆö the real struct is `[task][bank][src][dst][len]` at `sp+0/2/4/6/8` (the args sit *immediately* after the task id). The old code read `src=sp+6/dst=sp+8/len=sp+10`, skipping `src` by one word ŌåÆ it read a bogus `len=$EB6D` (60 KB) and scribbled the `$05xx` VM stack (THE cause of the old "$EF76 frame-marker" crash, AND why the populate only ever reproduced 2 bytes). Verified against the AFE1 cell-copy: `bank=4 src=$AA38(=$A57E+off) dst=frame-local len=1` ŌĆö i.e. it reads one metatile byte at a time from the **bank-4 `$A57E` table** (so `$A57E` is live after all, as the per-cell source, not the disproven whole-map renderer).
  3. **6502 `SBC (zp),Y` `$F1` + `(zp,X)` `$E1` were missing** from `cpu6502.py` ŌĆö added.
  - Remaining ~11% of the grid (108 bytes) + the 60 pre-`$7BFD` chrome bytes are written by the **render/decoration phase**, not the populate (they appear only in the full `AFE1` run, which now runs end-to-end with no crash, stopping only on the op budget). No regression: cpu6502 / dispatcher / math32 tests all still pass.
  - **NEXT:** decode the populated `$7BFD` grid to terrain types and confirm the Mino 15-clear/26-forest/12-mountain count (the final ground-truth check); then characterize the render-phase overlay (the other 11%) if a full-fidelity buffer is wanted.
- [~] 3. **ROMŌåÆMap PROVEN 2026-05-30 ŌĆö inputs pinned, no SRAM capture needed.** `$8903`'s *entire* input set: SRAM `$6F63/$6F64` (province) + `$6D9D/$6D9E` (=17, scenario fief-count / 17-vs-50 selector); ROM `$F70E[province]`ŌåÆmap_id (bank 15) and `$A57E + map_id├Ś55` cell pool (bank 4); **zero RAM inputs; mode `$6FFE` is render-only, not a populate input.** `$F70E[0..16] = [15,9,13,20,21,17,19,23,22,31,26,27,25,30,32,14,24]` (provinceŌåÆmap_id; Mino=8ŌåÆ22; pool has Ōēź33 maps). **Validated:** a *blank* SRAM seeded with only province=8 + `$6D9D`=17 reproduces the Mino grid **byte-for-byte (1027/1027)** vs the SaveRam-seeded run. None of `$6D9D`/`$F70E`/`$A57E` are in `mesen-labels.toml` yet ŌĆö add them.
  - **TOOL BUILT 2026-05-30: `render-rom-to-map.py <province>`** ŌĆö seeds `$6F63`+`$6D9D` ŌåÆ runs `$8903` ŌåÆ hands `$7BFD` to `render-from-sram`'s decoder. Render step is **Path A** (see Inbox PPU ticket for deferred Path B). Loop 0ŌĆō16 ŌåÆ full 17-fief atlas from ROM alone (do this once 50-fief is settled, to avoid re-runs).
  - [x] **50-fief CONFIRMED 2026-05-30 (Tanba live test).** Blind ROM render of Tanba (province **29**, `--scenario 50`) ran **clean (`ok=True`, NO new/TODO syscall needed)** and matched the actual captured battle dump (`TanmbaBattle.dmp`) **55/55 decoded cells**. ### EPIC: AI turn, TOP-DOWN (the "how does the AI choose" decode ŌĆö like the player command-list chapter)
> Chris's framing (2026-05-30): stop spelunking mid-level subs; find "start of AI turn" and work DOWN through all the logic. The AI reuses the SAME command-driver table ($B9B2) as the player menu, so *issuing* a chosen command is trivial ŌĆö the interesting part is *how commands/targets are chosen*. Skeleton found this session:
> ```
> vm_bootstrap ($A778, bank 0)              ŌåÉ post-RESET; BECOMES the main game loop
>  Ōö£ŌöĆ daimyo_turn_order ($6F0B)             ŌåÉ per-season permutation, re-randomized; READ IN NATIVE CODE (not bytecode!)
>  Ōö£ŌöĆ sub_A455 ($A455)                      ŌåÉ weakness-mark planner (sets daimyo_weakness_flag $6DD4, health-weighted)
>  Ōö£ŌöĆ call_bank(1)  [sub_CBB1 = syscall 7]  ŌåÉ bank 1 = TURN PROCESSOR (player input + AI executor)
>  ŌööŌöĆ call_bank(2)                          ŌåÉ bank 2 = combat resolution
> ```
> Why mid-level subs ($B79B issuer, $B89B/$B8A0 per-fief driver) had NO direct callers: they're in bank 1, reached via **call_bank(1)** (cross-bank, indirect) + the **$B9B2 driver table** (CALLPTR). The decompiler can't see those edges; that's why bottom-up stalled.
- [x] **1. Bank-1 turn-processor root FOUND 2026-05-30.** Native `$8000` (bank 1) = `4C 9B B8` = **`JMP $B89B`**. So `call_bank(1)` runs **`sub_B89B`** (body `$B8A0`) ŌĆö the per-fief driver IS the turn root. (Native disasm `disasm/bank_01_labeled.asm` is the tool for these trampolines, not the bytecode decompile.)
- [x] **3. AI executor chain MAPPED 2026-05-30** (did this before 2, the calls revealed it):
> ```
> sub_B89B (turn root)  ŌĆö loops provinces local11=0..fief_count:
>   per province (selected_province_idx):
>     - $6DA1 AI-budget counter ++/-- (read+write each step; the per-turn action budget?)
>     - war_helper_d972(prov) && rng_mod(4)   ŌåÆ weakness-war check (daimyo_weakness_flag gate, 25%)
>     - board checks sub_D628 / sub_D982 / sub_D609
>     - switch $6CF7[prov] (per-province STATE 0-5)
>     - CALL $B79B ($B989)  ŌåÉ command issuer
>         ŌåÆ if rest_turns_remaining[$6D67][daimyo] != 0: consume rest, skip
>         ŌåÆ else: loop sub_B6B4() pick cmd-idx ŌåÆ command_driver_table[$B9B2][idx] ŌåÆ run driver (SAME as player menu)
>             sub_B6B4 ŌåÆ sub_D14E (cursor/menu-item engine; reads controller via syscall 6 = read_controller)
> ```
> So the AI issues commands through the EXACT player path ($B6B4ŌåÆ$B9B2 driver), confirming Chris's "AI uses the same map." `$6CF7` = per-province action-state (0-5); `$6DA1` = an AI counter manipulated every step (budget/aggression ŌĆö pin its exact role next). `$B875`/`$B3AA`/`$B4D5` (maybe-train / AI-send / recruit) are likely $B9B2-table targets reached via the driver dispatch, not separate top-level calls.
- [~] **2. Player-vs-AI fork ŌĆö ANSWERED via Lua trace 2026-05-31 (ai-turn-trace.lua).** A 17-fief Miyoshi(d14) game traced `selected_province_idx` ($6F5F) writes: each turn has **Phase A** = a fast deterministic INDEX-order sweep over a fixed ~11-province set (~7 frames, gap 0-1 = an automated SYSTEM batch, candidate economy/harvest or the weakness planner) then **Phase B** = slow SHUFFLED-order processing (gaps), owners spanning d0-d16 with the **player's province interspersed among AI daimyo** = the per-daimyo TURN LOOP in randomized `daimyo_turn_order`. So **player + AI share ONE unified turn loop; the fork is INTERNAL** (player slot ŌåÆ read_controller in sub_D14E; AI slot ŌåÆ same code auto-resolves). Gate flag = the `mem_7FE7`-family in sub_D14E (exact bit not yet pinned). **MECHANIC FOUND:** `syscall_read_controller` sets `skip_wallclock` ($0089) while a button is held ŌåÆ game-time/RNG PAUSES during player input ŌĆö so the trace's giant frame-gaps (670/1347/2740) are real-time with the clock frozen (menu deliberation + battle animation), NOT AI compute; moderate ~20-30f gaps = AI auto-resolving, clock running. Caveat: $6F5F is overloaded (turn-index AND UI cursor), so the exact fork bit needs sub_D14E static work or a `skip_wallclock` probe.
- [ ] **2b (optional). Pin the exact fork bit** ŌĆö hook `skip_wallclock` ($0089) writes (set = player input active) + log `selected_province_idx`, OR static-decode the `mem_7FE7` branch in sub_D14E.
- [ ] **2-LEGACY. Player-vs-AI fork ŌĆö (superseded by 2 above).** The player and AI share `sub_B89B ŌåÆ $B79B ŌåÆ sub_B6B4 ŌåÆ sub_D14E`; the fork (read controller for player vs auto-select for AI) is inside the **menu/cursor engine** (`sub_D14E`, gated by mode flags `mem_7FE7`/`mem_6F79`/`$7FE1`), which is intricate UI code. **Pin it empirically:** Lua write-callback on `selected_province_idx` ($6F5F) + a flag like `$7FE7`, watch which provinces hit `read_controller` (only the player's should). Cleaner than static-decoding the cursor engine. (Turn-ORDER iteration over `daimyo_turn_order` $6F0B is still native ŌĆö separate.)
- [~] **4. War target-selection chain MAPPED 2026-05-31 ŌĆö and it's OWNERSHIP-based, not strength-based (surprise).** `driver_war ($9850) ŌåÆ province_select_helper ($879F) ŌåÆ sub_8172 (candidate filter) ŌåÆ sub_812F (per-mode dispatch) ŌåÆ sub_D9B7 (leaf: `fief_to_daimyo_map[cand] == enemy` ŌĆö OWNERSHIP check)`. Candidates are filtered by **adjacency + enemy-ownership + `$6CF7[fief] != 0xFF`** (per-province state gate); `sub_8172` returns the COUNT of valid candidates. **NO troop-`men` comparison in target selection.** Ō¤╣ REFRAMES the Mutsu invasion: the AI does NOT cherry-pick weak fiefs ŌĆö it picks among adjacent enemy fiefs, and weak ones fall because they LOSE the battle (combat-outcome, not smart targeting). The user's "low troops" instinct was right about the OUTCOME, wrong about the mechanism. **OPEN:** (a) the AI's pick AMONG multiple valid candidates (random? weakness-flag? first?) ŌĆö not yet located; (b) confirm the combat-strength resolution (bank 2). **TESTABLE:** if combat-outcome, the AI should sometimes attack a STRONGER fief and LOSE; if smart-targeting, it only attacks fiefs it outguns. Lua/play test: do AI attacks ever fail?
>   - **EMPIRICAL (2026-05-31, ai-war-target{2,3,4}.lua, 17-fief Miyoshi=d14):** the AI DOES have a target preference (not random) ŌĆö it attacks WEAK (low-men) adjacent enemies. Of the clean AI-vs-AI committed battles (isolating real commits by `$6F63` staying stable Ōēź30 frames, filtering out player-turn artifacts where `$6F63` idles on the player's fief): **3 of 4 hit the min-men adjacent neighbor** (f8ŌåÆf4=94, f16ŌåÆf8=90, f15ŌåÆf8=38), one did NOT (f7ŌåÆf8=218 over weaker f16=48). So **"prefer weak, but NOT strict argmin"** ŌĆö likely a winnability ratio (attacker men vs defender men) or strategic value as the real rule, not absolute minimum. `wk` (weakness-mark) was 0 on essentially all targets (marking is rare, ~4%/turn) so it's NOT the target driver. **CONFIRMED 2026-05-31 (ai-war-target4, 6 turns / 5 clean AI battles + earlier): AI attacks its WEAKEST-MEN adjacent enemy ŌĆö 6 of 8 = exact min ŌĆö and does so EVEN WHEN OUTNUMBERED** (min-men attacks at attacker/defender ratio 0.78, 0.71). So **winnability is REFUTED**: the rule is about the TARGET's weakness, not the attacker's advantage. Ō¤╣ AI attacks the weakest neighbor and combat resolves on strength separately, which is WHY AI attacks sometimes FAIL. This is the complete answer to "why OdaŌåÆMino / why my 13-man Mutsu fell" ŌĆö weakest adjacent enemy. The ~1/5 exceptions (chose a higher-men target over an available weaker one) ŌåÆ refinement OPEN: (a) the real metric may be army POWER (men├Śmorale├Śarms), not raw men, or (b) the weaker fief was unattackable (pact/alliance). The candidate FILTER is ownership+adjacency+$6CF7 (driver_war chain); the SCORER = this weakest-men preference (located empirically; static locus still open ŌĆö the AI auto-select branch). **Ō¢Č Optional NEXT: add morale+arms (army power) to the logger to test the exceptions.**
>   - **METHOD CORRECTION 2026-05-31 (Chris): STOP probe-guessing, READ the C.** v5's men-decrease trigger logged NOTHING across 6 battles ŌĆö premise wrong (the WINNER KEEPS the fief's men/gold/rice, so the defender's men can INCREASE on conquest). Three probe iterations spent guessing a signal. Pivoted to reading the decompiled C (the project's actual method) + LABELING as we go (Layer-2). **CODE-READ FINDING: the AI target-selection chain has NO troop-`men` comparison ŌĆö it's pure ELIGIBILITY filtering:** `driver_war ŌåÆ province_select_helper ŌåÆ count_eligible_targets ($8172) [+ target_eligible_by_cmd $812F + is_enemy_owned $D9B7 + province_state_is_FF $D999]`; `combat_helper_dd3a` filters then calls `syscall16_sram_wrap` (plumbing). The gate is **`province_ai_state` ($6CF7, per-province 0-5/0xFF)**, NOT men. Ō¤╣ the empirical "weakest-men" (6/8) was **emergent or probe-noise** (that data had confirmed false positives: player-fief idle + before/after double-fires), NOT explicitly coded. Labeled the read subs ($8172/$812F/$8DE1/$D9B7/$D999/$CBBD/$6CF7) ŌåÆ propagated to readable C. **Ō¢Č REAL NEXT (code-walk, not Lua): what WRITES `province_ai_state` non-zero?** Main setter is `sub_98A3` ($98BF: `$6CF7[fief]=arg3`, on ownership change); enumerate its callers + the state values 0-5 to find whether targetability is conquest/event/men-based. That's the actual "how the AI chooses" answer.
>   - **WALKED TO THE BOTTOM 2026-05-31 (code-read, not probes): there is NO AI target-scorer.** The full war-target chain is `driver_war ŌåÆ province_select_prompt ($804C) ŌåÆ select_province_by_cursor ($D59D) ŌåÆ cursor_nav_loop ($D3ED) ŌåÆ sub_D14E (NES button decode, bits 1/2/16/32/64/128 ŌĆö SAME as the player menu)`, gated by eligibility (`is_enemy_owned $D9B7` + `province_ai_state $6CF7 != 0xFF`). It **bottoms out in controller input** ŌĆö the AI selects its target by driving the IDENTICAL menu/cursor machinery the human uses (vindicates "the AI uses the same map" at the deepest level). So "weakest-men" / "OdaŌåÆMino" is **NOT a coded scorer** ŌĆö it's emergent from eligibility + cursor navigation (+ the earlier probe data had false positives). Labeled the chain ($804C/$D59D/$D3ED/$8172/$812F/$8DE1/$D9B7/$D999/$6CF7) ŌåÆ readable C. **Ō¢Č LAST GAP: `sub_D14E`'s AI branch** ŌĆö when it's the AI's turn, what feeds the "button"/cursor (synthetic input? auto-confirm on first eligible? RNG?). That's the only remaining locus of any actual AI "decision" in target selection.
- **NATIVE-CODE WRINKLE:** turn-order iteration + player/AI branch are native 6502, NOT VM bytecode ŌĆö the bytecodeŌåÆC decompiler is blind to them. This epic may need a native-6502 read of the bank-1 `$8000` entry and/or live Lua tracing, not just `decompiled/`.

## Done ŌĆö recent (newest first; trim to ~15, full history is in chapters + git)
- **VM teardown task "A" ŌĆö table-driven dispatch (family consolidation)** (2026-06-03) ŌĆö collapsed the ~50 mechanical opcode arms in `vm_decompile.py` into 3 data tables + 2 generic blocks (`_BINOP` with signedness-cast field, `_UNARY_A` templates, `_op_hex`/`_op_int` operand helpers). Net ŌłÆ45 lines; dropped a dead duplicate `div` arm. Genuinely-distinct handlers (host_call/switch/ext_op/frame-access/branches) stay explicit by design. Pure refactor: decompiled C byte-identical, all gates green. Skipped task "B" (0-site opcode `verified=` flags = deferred cross-game spec-completeness, not a blocker). [[feedback_high_quality_code_not_more_code]]
- **VM teardown task "C" ŌĆö positive-arg rendering + real arity** (2026-06-03) ŌĆö `vm_decompile.py` `_slot_name` now names arg5+ (positive odd `fp+N`) and the byte-arg subs the quick opcodes can't reach; `_body_arg_count` counts general-opcode arg reads (word+byte) so 13 subs get correct arity (the 6-arg blit wrappers, `scaled_transfer_da24`, `char_classify`/`is_lower`/ŌĆ” text engine). Last raw `fp+N` eliminated. Migrated one stranded far-key (`dedup_buf` fp-14ŌåÆlocal5). All gates green. Teardown's "reads naturally" goal met for args. (ROADMAP Inbox ticket, struck.)
- **DECOMPILER: discarded calls now emitted as statements (+1418 calls recovered)** (2026-06-01, commit `6ddd876`) ŌĆö the VM is a stack machine; `vm_decompile.py` parked each `host_call`/`CALL` result in `regA` and only emitted it if something CONSUMED `regA` before the next write. Side-effecting calls whose result was discarded vanished silently ŌåÆ `vm_bootstrap`/`render_boot_title_screens`/victory screen/all boot+UI funcs read as empty loops. Fix: `regA` is now a property that flushes a pending call as `func();` on unconsumed overwrite (+ before unconditional `goto` + at function end), tagged with the call's own address. Recovered +1418 call statements (bank_00 +368 / 01 +661 / 02 +326 / 15 +145). Validated: `effect_grow` byte-IDENTICAL, every added line a call stmt, the 18 changed lines are `goto`ŌåÆbraces re-folds that ALSO recovered dropped calls (one fixed a real bug ŌĆö missing `effect_war_a()` before a return in the AI attack path); re-run deterministic. **This was the biggest single readability win since decompile-all ŌĆö the boot/UI layer is now legible in C, no bytecode drop needed.** Surfaced while walking the boot sequence with Chris (the C looked like a bare AI-turn loop because the boot calls were dropped).
- **DAIMYO PORTRAITS LOCATED ŌĆö composite face system, bank 8** (2026-06-01, commit `d38ac80`) ŌĆö portraits are NOT stored whole; they're procedurally composed from base-5 face-code parts. `assign_unique_daimyo_face_code` ($DB97) rolls a unique base-5 word into `daimyo_face_code_table` ($6EB1[daimyo]); `compose_upload_daimyo_portrait` ($8086, bank 2) splits it into feature digits and uploads each feature's variant tiles from **bank 8** (`$A604` head / `$A9C4` eyes / `$ABA4` nose / `$AD84` mouth, 5 variants each, new `[prg.bank8]`) to CHR-RAM ŌåÆ a 6├Ś6 face. **VISUALLY VERIFIED** via new `tools/render-portrait.py` (faces render as recognizable daimyo) ŌåÆ `atlas/portrait-{sheet,faces}.png`. Bank pinned via the `ppu_upload_block` bank arg=8. Also fixed 4 rom-xref cross-bank-pointer false positives (filed under bank 2, data is bank 8). Feeds the visual-atlas chapter. [[project_nobunaga_daimyo_portraits]] **Open polish:** exact part-blockŌåÆnametable layout (the 6├Ś6 tile arrangement) is approximated, not pinned.
- **"SEE THE WHOLE PICTURE" EPIC essentially COMPLETE** (2026-05-30) ŌĆö `tools/decompile-all.py` persists `decompiled/bank_{00,01,02,15}.c`: the entire engine's bytecode (495 subs, ~11.8k lines) as readable C, **byte-deterministic**. The 3-step pipeline that took the whole tooling-discipline arc to enable now runs end-to-end: ROM ŌåÆ vm-disasm.py (execution-validated lengths) ŌåÆ vm_decompile.py (opcode-keyed dispatch) ŌåÆ committed C. Reading the engine is now opening a file. Remaining: commit to git; raise decompiler coverage (22% TODO ŌåÆ lower by decoding more opcode semantics). See `decompiled/README.md`.
- **`vm_decompile.py` made spec-agnostic** (2026-05-30) ŌĆö the keystone debt from the vm-disasm recovery. Dispatch now normalizes mnemonics from the **opcode byte** (not the spec-specific name string), so the decompiler reads old OR new (v2) disasm interchangeably. Closed via an opcodeŌåÆcanonical-name table + matching the signed-decimal immediate rendering in vm-disasm. **Validated by a confusion matrix on bank 1:** decompile output differs old-vs-new **iff** the sub contains a length-fixed opcode (49) or a relabeled address (24); 58 subs byte-identical; 0 false either way; grow's formula reproduces exactly. The decompiler is no longer coupled to the (partially-buggy) old files' naming ŌĆö EPIC step 3b (decompile-all) is unblocked.
- **`vm-disasm.py` RECOVERED + EPIC reframed** (2026-05-30) ŌĆö the bulk VM disassembler that had drifted out of `tools/`. Rebuilt on the **execution-validated** `nobunaga_vm.OPCODE_INFO` (not the deleted old spec), with handler-decoded `$D5`/`$D9` variable-length inline jump tables and recursive-descent reachability termination. Validated by an artifact-independent **exact-tiling** test (the `JSR $E823` stub list must tile each bank): **0 misaligned / 495 subs** on banks 0/1/2/15. Two findings fell out: **(a)** the old `_vm.asm` files had **wrong operand lengths** for ~10 opcodes ($84/$86/$88, $A0-$A3, $AA, $AF, $DE/$DF) ŌĆö proven by emulator `vm_pc`-delta probes + ROM handler reads; the old authors were mid-hand-correction (their own comments say "classifier mis-sizedŌĆ”") and never finished; `OPCODE_INFO` is right. **(b)** **banks 03-14 are ~all DATA** (0 bytecode stubs except bank 10=1, bank 14=3) ŌåÆ the whole engine's *code* is just banks 0/1/2/15, already dumped. The external sources (NESDEV t=15931, NovaSquirrel `sea16-reference.c`) are a **different VM revision** (offset opcode map: their `$a0`=deref = our `$B0`) and can't arbitrate this ROM ŌĆö only its own handlers can. See the reframed "See the whole picture" EPIC.
- **Map populator `$8903` cracked** (2026-05-30) ŌĆö `call_bank ($07)` implemented (re-entrant native `$8000` runner with `$F226` interception), a long-standing `memcpy_banked` param-offset bug fixed (struct is `[task][bank][src][dst][len]` at sp+0/2/4/6/8; old code skipped `src`, read a 60 KB length, scribbled the VM stack ŌĆö root cause of the "$EF76" crash and the 2-byte populate), and missing 6502 `SBC ($F1/$E1)` opcodes added. Result: `$8903` runs clean and reproduces **880/988 (89%)** of the Mino cell grid. `$A57E` (bank 4) is the live per-cell metatile source. No regression. See the 50-fief EPIC step 2'.
- **Kernel syscall layer promoted into `nobunaga_vm`** (2026-05-30) ŌĆö intercepts `host_call $F226`, dispatches the 23-entry `$C173` table by task id (read from `vm_sp`; bank-switch emulated by reading the target ROM page directly). **16/23 resolved:** 6 emulated (memcpy_banked, rng, set_sprite, palette_write, palette_swap, audio_load_voice), 10 stubbed (PPU/audio/input/nmi-wait/chr ŌĆö moot headless). No regression (cpu6502/dispatcher tests + math32 still exact). Bytecode no longer hangs on syscalls. See [[project_nobunaga_emulator_tools]].
- **math32 ext-op blocker CRACKED** (2026-05-29) ŌĆö `pct_op`/`math32_3arg`/`math32_2arg` derived + emulator-verified via `probe-math32.py`. The standing magnitude blocker across Dam/AI/combat is gone; the B7 table stayed unopened (helpers were the real interface).
- **Tooling-discipline meta-project COMPLETE** (2026-05-29) ŌĆö registration layer (CONTEXT + 3 registries), `/nobunaga` skill, script consolidation (ŌłÆ11/+2, every merge output-verified), trace gzip (2.9 GBŌåÆ250 MB lossless), data-provenance system + `data-index.py auto` (145 legacy dumps contextualized ŌåÆ backlog clean). The anti-drift thesis applied to its own toolchain.

## How to use this file
End each session by asking the [[notes/claude-code-skill-engineering]] compounding question, applied to *plans*: did anything move? Promote/park/close items here. An item that's been in **Open** for many sessions with no progress is a signal ŌĆö either it's blocked on one thing (name it) or it's actually Parked (be honest).
